    Collection of Medical Works from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 448

    Pediatric Dysentery

    Hejian's Six Writings (By Liu Wanshu)

    Dysentery

    Children suffering from spleen dysfunction and dysentery have significant heat. Sudden shock can cause dysentery with a greenish color, indicating heat as a proving factor. What about yellow dysentery? It arises when fire is excessive, causing water to decline and spleen function to be strong, leading to yellow dysentery. If the dysentery is red, it signifies deep heart fire, indicating severe heat; if the dysentery is black, it results from extreme heat where it combines with water's transformative effects, causing a black color.[1p]

    Confucianism and Caring for Parents by Zhang Congzheng

    Dysentery

    For children suffering from prolonged diarrhea, particularly around eight or nine months, it is often due to deep autumn-related cold dysentery, characterized by greenish-white diarrhea and occasional painful cramps. If there are unresolved milk phlegm issues, you may use Yin Pi Wan (Spleen Nourishing Pills) the size of a millet grain, taking 20 to 30 pills each time, washed down with rice drink, administered three times a day for recovery. Additionally, Yiyuang (a medicinal herb) can also be used.

    Complete Medical Book for Infants by Zhu Zhenheng

    Dysentery

    Dysentery, regardless of being red or white, is associated with damp-heat. Some may mistakenly perceive the white type as cold; this is incorrect. It can also occur due to food accumulation. Treatment involves both strengthening and purging therapies. In cases of dysentery, whether red or white, both dampness and heat are usually present. However, hot conditions feature abdominal pain, while damp conditions do not cause pain.

    For red dysentery, damp-heat injures the blood aspect, coming from the small intestine. The treatment method is to use Si Wu Decoction with the addition of Huang Lian (Coptis), Huang Qin (Scutellaria), and Huang Bai (Phellodendron). For white dysentery, damp-heat injures the qi aspect, coming from the large intestine. The treatment method is to use Si Jun Zi Decoction with the addition of Huang Lian and Cang Zhu (Atractylodes).

    For cases of mixed red and white dysentery, both blood and qi have been injured, requiring Ba Zhen Decoction with the addition of Huang Lian, Huang Qin, Huang Bai, Huashi (Talc), and Cang Zhu for treatment.

    In these three cases, if the symptoms are severe, add Bing Lang (Areca) and Zhi Ke (Bitter Orange).

    For treating dysentery, regardless of color, during the initial phase, if there is urgency followed by heaviness, and abdominal distention with pain, first use San Huang Wan to purge; if severe, use Cheng Qi Decoction, followed by Xiang Lian Wan to supplement.[2p]
    For chronic red and white dysentery, when the person is weak and has not previously taken laxatives, if one administers laxatives, the person will feel empty and weak, which is detrimental. If laxatives are not given, the accumulation will not dissipate and recovery will be difficult. One should use Baohuan pills repeatedly for several doses, gauging treatment by the alleviation of abdominal pain; afterwards, use Xianglian pills for adjustment.

    In treating dysentery, one must never recklessly use poisonous drugs like ba dou or qian niu; instead, the use of Sanhuang pills is advised.

    For dysentery accompanied by fresh blood, the treatment is to use Qingxue pills and take a decoction of plantain herb and roasted old rice, which is remarkably effective.

    For white saliva in dysentery that does not stop for a long time, use Guichang pills and take them with a controlled amount of brewed old rice, which is notably effective.

    For red and white dysentery that persists for a long time, use Ergeng pills and take them with brewed old rice for immediate effect.

    For pure red dysentery in summer, roast Yiyuan powder with talcum powder and add red yeast to make pills, taking them with brewed old rice.

    In cases of red and white dysentery with rectal prolapse, this indicates downward energy, so one should lift and support it using Hezhong pills followed by Shengma decoction.

    For red and white dysentery with thirst, Bai Zhu powder should be used as the main treatment.[3p]
    For those suffering from dysentery with symptoms of red and white diarrhea, vomiting, and loss of appetite, this condition is called "silent mouth dysentery." If treated with wood fragrance, it will lead to warmth-loss, and if with yam, it will lead to closure. One should use a formula of ginseng, poria, and white atractylodes powder, mixed with decocted rice water, to ease the chest, making the person naturally desire food.

    In the case of an infant with this condition, one can use fresh fetal feces, place it in a small ceramic jar, add a little musk and a small amount of mercury, mix well, and store. For a child with silent mouth dysentery, applying this medicine into the eyes two or three times is remarkably effective.

    After dysentery has ceased, if there is still fever and weakness, one should use the Jisheng pill. If the dysentery persists for a long time, accompanied by high fever and great thirst, it is untreatable. If the six pulses are rapid and strong, the face is red and the body weak, it is untreatable. If there is vomiting and lack of appetite despite medication, it is untreatable. If the condition has persisted for a long time, resulting in purple blood with clots, it is untreatable. If there is black water resembling dust from a leaking roof, it is untreatable. If dysentery turns into seizures, it is untreatable. If after dysentery, it changes into diarrhea while diet remains normal, it is untreatable. If there is prolonged unquenchable thirst and gradual decrease in food intake, it is untreatable. If the hands and feet are emaciated, and large amounts of flesh are lost, it is untreatable. If there is anal prolapse of an inch that cannot be reduced, it is untreatable.

    All the above conditions are long-standing dysentery; those who exhibit these symptoms are beyond help.[4p]
    The ancestral tradition treats dysentery. Without distinguishing between red and white, one first administers detoxifying pills, then uses Xianglian pills to adjust the condition.

    Dysentery was formerly known as "stagnation and diarrhea," caused by accumulated food and damp heat. Symptoms include bowel sounds and pain, making it hard to find comfort, with urgency and a feeling of heaviness inside without a clear side. Red indicates excessive heat in the small intestine, while white signifies the evil invading the large intestine. Inept physicians mistakenly treat white as cold, using pungent and hot herbs chaotically.

    Initially, there are no two methods for treating dysentery, as the secret of Hejian is passed down. The techniques of regulating qi and harmonizing blood should be prioritized, with a focus on obtaining the root without deviation. Once qi is activated, the feeling of heaviness will cease, and the movement of blood must calm the dysentery. Avoid spicy and sweet flavors when treating cold and damp conditions, not fearing the passage of years or days.

    Generally, one should first administer purgatives such as Huanglian, Zhikua, and Binglang. Big Yellow should be steamed with alcohol, with Licorice and Mangxiao used nearby. If red and white dysentery persists for a long time, and the patient is weak and restless, Baohuo pills are the immortal remedy, requiring careful recognition of the illness.

    After the evacuation, pain and urgency should be alleviated, followed by a careful analysis of red and white symptoms. For red dysentery, do not exceed the use of the red formula; for white dysentery, it is safe and reliable for the intestines. If red and white symptoms coexist without improvement, Xianglian pills are highly effective. Renowned physicians spread their names across the four seas, achieving prominence atop a brocade crown.[5p]
    If encountering a seasonal dysentery, there is no difference in opening the door. Headaches, body heat, and slow sighing are to be feared in times of epidemics. First, use ginseng to dispel toxins, then apply purging methods. However, one must observe the pulse and adjust accordingly, distinguishing weakness from strength before stopping.

    If dysentery persists without cessation, the qi stagnates and the intestines become slippery. Urgently administer good medicine to reinforce and stabilize. Ginseng, angelica, and asarum, with black plum, buckwheat husks, and scutellaria. Dried ginger, chebula, red poria, with japonica rice and dried tangerine peel as a guide.

    Remember the medicinal items for dysentery—detoxifying with gardenia and scutellaria. The two substances of natron and realgar can promote transformation, while woody and green peels relieve pain. Bitter orange and betel nut for heaviness, and asarum and bupleurum can uplift. Strengthen the intestines with buckwheat husks and chebula, and use alisma and polyporus for smoothness.

    If dysentery is untreated, the symptoms will be numerous, with a pulse like a roaring river that must be guarded against. Withheld food leads to vomiting of watery fluids, high fever, thirst, irritability, and abdominal distention. The large orifice fails to contain the spirit, and feces appear like dark dust. Red face, red lips, sunken eyes, the qi is urgent and chaotic, resembling a state of death.[6p]
    Diarrhea

    In spring and autumn months, children are exposed to cold in the morning and evening. The cold air affects their limbs, and if heat cannot be released, it leads to strong heat. If cold air enters the stomach, it causes diarrhea, which may be red or white, appearing several times. Children may have abdominal distension and severe pain from the strong heat, with vigorous and rapid pulses. For those with heat, it is advisable to administer a regulating decoction; when the heat in the stools subsides, the diarrhea will also resolve. However, those with strong heat who do not vomit or have diarrhea should also take it.

    Additionally, in the summer months and early autumn, if exposed to sudden cold amidst intense heat, the body cannot disperse it, leading to internal turmoil. If it manifests externally, it results in malaria; if internally, it leads to diarrhea. When both conditions arise, malaria and diarrhea occur simultaneously, caused by disharmony in the protective and nutritive Qi, and weakness in the intestines and stomach, permitting cold and hot air to invade. This can also be due to dietary harm from unregulated cold and heat, where combined cold yields white, and combined heat yields red stools. If cold and heat attack together, pus and blood will be mixed; it can also be caused by accumulated heat resulting in red diarrhea, and accumulated cold resulting in white diarrhea, resulting in confusion between red and white and the accumulation of both cold and heat.[7p]
    If there is deficiency in the spleen and stomach qi, and they cannot digest food, then waste does not gather; or in spring, if released from discomfort, if harmed by cold winds, the intestines and stomach may weaken, and suddenly be afflicted by wind and cold, resulting in frequent diarrhea. The classics say: "If harmed by wind in spring, summer will certainly have diarrhea." For this, a formula regulating the middle can be used, removing rhubarb and adding bitter orange. If diarrhea does not stop, add yellow bitter to treat it. For sudden diarrhea, use powdered plantago seed, mixed with rice drink, which is also effective. In hot months, use Wuling powder or plantago seed powder, mixed with light heart soup; also use a modified version of the Fire-Purging powder. If there are joint diseases of Taiyang and Yangming, there will definitely be diarrhea, for which Gegen decoction is the main treatment. If accompanied by vomiting, add pinellia. Sijunzi decoction is also applicable.

    Concerning Various Types of Diarrhea

    Diarrhea in children often arises from excessive eating habits, or from eating fruits and meats without knowing when to stop. Thus, the spleen and stomach, still weak, cannot handle it, leading to accumulation in the organs, which causes diarrhea. If heat strikes, it will be red. If wind and cold enter the intestines and stomach, causing the current fluids to stagnate, it will result in white diarrhea. If it is accompanied by greenish discharge, it may be due to fright accumulation; or if it feels very painful in the stomach like brain of fish. Generally, the eight types of diarrhea are only distinguished by heat and cold, red and white. Even though the properties of the medicines may differ, the treatment methods are not far apart. If there is a mix of red and white, first eliminate the heat accumulation by using medicines like rhubarb, bitter orange, and sodium sulfate to remove heat and toxins; then employ yellow bitter, bitter chrysanthemum, and berberine to resolve the heat, thus stopping the diarrhea and alleviating the pain—this is a wonderful method. If the diarrhea does not stop, use prepared ephedra and other medicines for regulation, and it will naturally return to normal.[8p]
    For those with spleen deficiency, it is unwise to lightly use substances like grain husks and similar agents, as this could lead to danger and distress. One must use substances like mo stone, huanglian, ejiao, and diyu to stop it, which would be the best approach. The use of zhiqiao and shao yao is also essential. For dysentery with a closed mouth and inability to eat, Shilian San is the principal prescription, and Xiangpu San is also applicable. For cold dysentery with symptoms like abdominal pain akin to bean juice, Weifeng Tang is the remedy. When there is spleen toxin and a hot condition with dysentery, one should often take Xianglian Wan, Huanglian Xiangru Drink, remove Gui from Wuling San, use Maogen Tang, and incorporate Danggui, Shaoyao, Zhiqiao, Diyu, Chuanxiong, and other prescriptions to first detoxify and reduce heat, then to stimulate appetite and consume food, facilitating the drainage of water and grains. To relieve intestinal pain and loosen the bowels, one should first use water-soaked Dan, Baidu San, Diyu Drink, and a laxative mixture with Zhiqiao. In cases of persistent diarrhea with heat, Sanhuang Shun Ai Tang is the main prescription. If there is obstruction due to accumulation, Shenxiong may also be utilized. For severe heat and restlessness, Huanglian Jiedu Tang can resolve the condition, and Pohuosan is also effective.[9p]
    Medical Overview by Lou Ying

    Dysentery

    Pediatric dysentery in children is generally caused by disharmony between the spleen and stomach, overindulgence in inappropriate foods, leading to stagnation that cannot be transformed. Additionally, it can be caused by a wet heat pathogen or by the nursing mother consuming excessive raw or overly rich foods and transmitting these effects. Symptoms arise also from the invasion of pathogenic factors like wind, warmth, and dampness. In cases where there is urgent abdominal pain, the nature of fire is rapid, which can dry out materials. Sometimes, at the end of summer or beginning of autumn, a sudden chill may invade internally without any means of dispersal, leading to conditions like malaria; if both internal and external symptoms manifest, it can result in dysentery-malaria.

    If dysentery persists for a long time, it can cause swelling and fullness, with the lower body being colder and the upper body having heat accumulation, resulting in a condition of excess above and deficiency below. In cases where there is damp heat toxicity affecting the spleen, it can lead to a blockage in the stomach, resulting in symptoms like locked jaw. There is also a possibility of family transmission, where the young and old show similar symptoms, indicating an epidemic dysentery. Treatment should first consider the seasonal changes to balance external factors, examine stagnation to regulate internal conditions, carefully assess the nature of injuries, and distinguish between excess and deficiency, as well as hot and cold conditions, to provide effective treatment without arbitrary interventions.[10p]
    Red and White Dysentery

    Regarding red and white dysentery, people generally say that red represents Yang and heat, while white represents Yin and cold; some even assert that without accumulation, dysentery cannot occur. However, when it comes to treatment, if one were to alternate between hot and cold medicines or use laxatives to remove accumulation, it would be difficult to achieve effective results. Without understanding the underlying causes, how can one expect to treat it? Moreover, during the changing of the seasons and among various winds, the interplay of the five movements and six atmospheres leads people to suffer from dysentery, particularly in summer and autumn. The "Neijing" states: "In spring, one is harmed by wind; in summer, one suffers from diarrhea." The "Treatise on True Principles" says: "Lesser Yang is in the springs, defeated by excessive fire, causing the populace to suffer from red and white dysentery." Can one strictly adhere to the idea that without accumulation, dysentery cannot occur? If one only considers accumulation, then is it not the case that during summer and autumn, many suffer from it, while in spring and winter, this is not the same? It is indeed the case that pathogenic wind enters the stomach, where wood can overcome earth. If it does not lead to violent diarrhea, it results in dysentery, characterized by a mixture of red and white, indicating a lack of distinction between Yin and Yang.

    The proper method should clarify the distinction between Yin and Yang, using Wuling San to guide the counterflow, and Lirong Tang to warm the stomach, allowing the colors to harmonize before applying treatment. If after this differentiation, red and white continue to descend together, then one must investigate the root cause of the ailment. If white appears first, followed by red, it indicates internal injury from cold, resulting from failing to keep covered, with the primal energy affected by summer heat. The treatment should first save the interior, followed by dispelling the heat toxin. If red appears first and is then followed by white, it indicates that heat has harmed first, followed by loss of coverage leading to cold. The priority should be to relieve the heat, then treat the dysentery.[11p]
    If there is a hot dysentery, it will expel pure fresh blood. This condition can cause blood movement, so it is advisable to take cold preparations such as Huanglian Xiangru San, Chuan Cao San, and Danggui San. Additionally, add vinegar and stir-fry steamed cypress leaves, and take it as a decoction with ginger water, or use Qianghuo San combined with Sanhe Decoction, prepared with ginger and millet water.

    If there is a cold dysentery, it will expel pure white mucus, or it may appear pale with a hint of pink, or resemble purplish blood like that of a pig's liver. All these are signs of a yin condition, as cold can obstruct the blood. First, use Wuling San combined with Shouzhong Decoction and decoct it, then follow with Fuzi Lizhong Decoction and take it warm, or use Guzhen Decoction. If one cannot distinguish the deficiencies of yin and yang or the hot and cold conditions and mistakenly administer treatment, it will result in further weakening of the spleen and stomach, leading to an inability to digest food, or may even cause lockjaw dysentery, which is difficult to treat.

    Additionally, if there is urgency in the abdomen followed by heaviness at the back, it indicates urgency in the yang and heaviness in the yin. Abdominal pain before defecation indicates urgency, while pain after defecation indicates heaviness. Therefore, in cases of urgency, it is due to diarrhea in the large intestine. First, take Daxun Drink combined with Kuangqi Drink for resolution, along with Qianghuo San, prepared with ginger and millet water; then use Kuan Chang Wan. For heaviness, which indicates qi deficiency, combine Wuling San with ginseng and ginger and take as a decoction, and also administer Xianglian Wan. Ifboth conditions occur together, the first two pills can be administered together, or Baijin Drink or Jinsu Wan are also good options. However, diarrhea and dysentery are two distinct conditions: when watery stools mixed with feces are abundant and come easily, it is called diarrhea; when blood-stained white mucus comes in small amounts and is painful, it is called dysentery.[12p]
    The differentiation of light and heavy, yin and yang, is the basis of treatment methods. When there is a mixture of pus and blood that does not stop for a long time, varying between light during the day and heavy at night, or frequent during both day and night, with reduced appetite and increased pain, one should use Wanjin powder or Shenyxiao powder to address it.

    If there is a five-colored diarrhea, it is due to accumulated heat in the five internal organs, persisting for a long time, resulting in this condition. When the five organs receive heat, the nutritive and defensive qi become unbalanced, leading to improper digestion of grains, which corrupts the internal organs, causing the spirit to feel dull. At this point, it is quite dangerous, especially with sharp abdominal pain, and those who are small children have no treatment method. The five colors signify that the colors of the five organs are all visible on the surface. For older children, one may use the standard formula San Shen Wan or Xiao Lai Fu Dan, combined with Wuling powder for administration. If the medicines continue to be ineffective, one should not administer them further.

    Additionally, there is a wind diarrhea, mostly yellow-brown in color, which closely resembles malnutrition diarrhea but can be distinguished by the lack of foul smell. This wind poison stagnates in the spleen, requiring the removal of wind toxin from the spleen channel, with Xie Huang powder as the main treatment. If one observes both red and white substances being expelled together, and this continues without cessation, along with scant urine, simultaneous pain and heat symptoms, cracked lips and red eyes, shortness of breath with agitation, restlessness in sitting or lying down, extreme thirst for water, and food sinking within the body, combined with periodic facial appearances as if painted, along with lack of appetite, it is difficult to treat.

    Diarrhea with yellow, red, or black colors indicates heat; while diarrhea with blue or white indicates the inability to digest grains, suggesting cold conditions.[13p]
    The East Garden says: The white [discharge] indicates that damp heat injures the qi aspect; the red [discharge] indicates that damp heat injures the blood aspect; when red and white are mixed, both qi and blood are harmed. Haizang employs the Four Gentlemen Decoction, along with Chuanxiong and Angelica to treat weakness-related dysentery, and the Four Gentlemen Decoction with dry ginger for cold-related dysentery. I often treat cases where the hands and feet are hot and the patient drinks cold as real heat, using the Xianglian Pill; for cases where the hands and feet are cold and the patient drinks hot, I consider it virtual cold, employing the Yigong Powder with Xianglian Pill. If there are also symptoms of body heaviness and limb pain, it indicates damp heat injuring the spleen, for which I use the Shengyang Yige Decoction. If urination is not smooth, indicating a lack of distinction between yin and yang, I use the Wuling Powder. If damp heat has subsided but the dysentery persists, it indicates sinking of spleen qi, and I use the Buzhong Yiqi Decoction, adding increased doses of Cimicifuga and Bupleurum. For dysentery accompanied by vomiting, or abdominal pain, it indicates spleen and stomach deficiency and cold, so I use the Yigong Powder with prepared ginger and costus. If it transforms into intermittent fever, it indicates liver defeating the spleen, for which I use the Liu Junzi Decoction with Bupleurum and Eclipta. If accumulation and stagnation has been resolved but dysentery continues, it indicates deficiency of spleen qi, and I use the Four Gentlemen Decoction with Xianglian Pill. If the condition is caused by a nursing mother consuming rich and heavy foods, leading the child to illness, one should identify the cause, treat the mother accordingly, and also consider symptoms of heat and cold dysentery, constipation, and abdominal pain. If there are accompanying exterior symptoms, it is necessary to release the exterior.

    For the treatment of dysentery, if one wishes to address accumulation, simply use official methods to consume robust pills which can treat accumulation while also alleviating dysentery, ensuring efficacy. Once accumulation has cleared, promptly use the Four Gentlemen Decoction with cardamom and Chebula to replenish, followed by taking thick intestine Xianglian Pills for effectiveness.[14p]
    Treatment of Dysentery with Cooling Herbs

    For treating red dysentery, use the Four Noble Ginsengs with red peony and angelica, and simmer together with a small amount of millet.

    Pure Blood Dysentery

    According to the teachings of the Chao family: when a child's dysentery resembles thick blood, this is red dysentery. It comes from extreme intestinal weakness, causing both fat and blood to flow out together. The "Shenghui" states that in children, blood dysentery arises when heat and toxins affect the blood, which then enters the large intestine. The blood circulates along with Qi through the meridians and organs, and there is usually no stagnation. However, if influenced by poisonous heat, and if the intestines are weak where blood seeps into them, this will lead to blood dysentery. The "Baojian" mentions that in children, intestinal heat causes fresh blood to come out during dysentery, similar to intestinal wind.

    Treatment of Cold Dysentery with Warm Herbs[15p]
    To treat white dysentery, mix equal parts of the Four Gentlemen with dried ginger reduced by half, and add a small amount of millet to cook together.

    White Pus Dysentery

    The "Ying Tong Bao Jian" discusses children's intestinal cold, which leads to white pus and abdominal pain.

    Mixed Pus and Blood Dysentery

    The "Sheng Hui" states: for children with pus and blood dysentery, it arises from toxic qi within the organs. When the blood heats up, it overflows and permeates into the large intestine, clashing with the fluids in the intestines, accumulating heat and becoming congealed. The blood transforms into pus; hence, if the abdomen is weak, diarrhea results, leading to pus and blood dysentery. The "Ge Shi Zhu Hou" states: children’s internal toxins stagnate like fish brains.

    Five-Color Dysentery

    The "Xing Zheng Lun" sings: Five-color dysentery has many manifestations; knowing this, one understands the five types. The blue color signifies shock and accumulation; yellow indicates excess food accumulation in the spleen. White signifies cold weakness in the intestines and stomach; red indicates intense accumulated heat that is difficult to pacify. Chicken liver hidden accumulation forms patches; with mixed black blood, it is hard to stabilize. Lips chapped, chest elevated, exposing teeth; the face red with veins protruding always in front. Urgently pacify the organs with herbal decoctions; physicians must pay attention as the ancient sages taught.

    Another song states: Do not regard five-color dysentery as strange; it appears in children under four years old. Blue arises from shock accumulation; yellow from food toxicity in the spleen. Red and black indicate heart and kidney issues; white indicates harm mainly to the spleen. Before the age of three, there is no fluctuation; do not allow excessive sleeping or late meals.

    This illness requires harmonizing the five organs and nourishing the defensive and nutritive qi for gradual recovery. If the eyes are swollen and the diet is not improved, only use Ping Wei San for supplementation.[16p]

    Gū Lì (Dysentery)

    The "Cháo Shì Bìng Yuán" states: In children, gū poison dysentery occurs when seasonal changes in cold and heat are unregulated, leading to toxic and harmful qi. Children are weakened and hurt by it, with evils clashing against blood and qi, entering the intestines and stomach. Toxic qi accumulates; if the large intestine is vacuous, it transforms into dysentery with blood. The color of the dysentery resembles coagulated blood like pieces of chicken or duck liver, which accompanies the dysentery. This is due to the excess of toxic heat, affecting the internal organs, resembling gū poisoning; hence it is called gū toxin dysentery.

    The "Shí Bì Jīng" states that the song of the spleen toxin dysentery goes: "Within the spleen, there is a toxin called pure yang. This is caused by the excessive heat from medicinal herbs hurting the body. It leads to many blockages in the large intestine and to abundant desiccated blood in the shriveled intestines. If the abdomen is windy and closed, it is hard to open one's eyes. The body heats up, the head feels warm, and the feet turn cold. The tongue is red and the chest is elevated—these are the signs to follow. There is much weeping and shortness of breath, resembling madness. First, one must resolve the heat and open the appetite. This is when good physicians apply their remedies."

    When the spleen suffers from heat accumulation and becomes toxic, the treatment should cool the spleen and then eliminate the accumulation. If the bones in the chest suddenly rise, leading to increased dyspnea, it is not treatable.

    The "Fèng Suǐ Jīng" annotation states: It is advisable to take Jīn Huá Sǎn and Xiāng Lián Wán.

    The "Xíng Zhèng Lùn" states that the wind toxin dysentery song highlights: "Among the eight types of dysentery, the wind transforms with difficulty, appearing like the thick juice of green grass. The toxic wind mixes with bean juice, adding excessive heat. The stomach is ruined, resembling pieces of chicken liver. There is no need to first purgative the accumulation; closing the eyelids and completely avoiding food is unbearable to see. If it returns to white dysentery, it must be purged. The viscera and bowels should frequently be warmed to restore their original state."[17p]
    Dysentery with Accompanying Symptoms

    "Chao's Disease Sources" states: In children, dysentery accompanied by thirst indicates a watery dysentery. When fluids are depleted and the organs are weak and dry, it leads to increased thirst. If urination is frequent, dysentery ceases when thirst is relieved; if urination is scant, and fluids don’t move into the small intestine, but instead seep into the intestines and stomach, thirst persists and dysentery continues. In such cases, the body will appear swollen, as the spleen qi is too weak to manage fluids, leading to eye pain as well. Children generally have heat in the upper burner; now, with dysentery, the lower burner is weak and the upper burner is hot, resulting in excessive qi and heat affecting the liver. Mr. Mao believes food injury to the spleen and stomach is the cause, and suggests starting with "Awakening the Spleen Powder" and "Harmony Qi Powder" for adjustment. After a day, use "Middle-Adjustment Drink" with "Milk Aroma Powder" and "Dragon Spit Paste" to restore health. Alternatively, simply making a juice from winter melon may also help.

    Emaciation

    Chao states: In children, when the intestines and stomach are weak and affected by wind and cold, it leads to dysentery. After the dysentery resolves, the spleen and stomach remain weak, and qi from grains is still low, resulting in emaciation.

    Swelling

    "Huiji" discusses the case of children experiencing swelling all over after dysentery. The verse states: "If cold dysentery is untreated for long, widespread swelling occurs as if blown up. A strong pulse indicates qi has turned to water, and firmness arises from accumulations." The best method is to smooth the qi to reduce swelling; after balancing qi for two days, frequent urination will establish. Avoid overeating to prevent stagnation, as this condition fundamentally stems from the damage to the spleen.[18p]
    Prolapse of the Anus

    The lungs and the large intestine are interrelated. The anus is the entrance of the large intestine. When the lungs are excessively hot, they obstruct and block; when the lungs are weak and cold, the rectum may protrude. This condition can arise from prolonged dysentery, resulting in urgency and forceful straining of the anus, which may be exposed to external wind, or from heat-induced diarrhea, where the intestines become loose and uncontrollable. Alternatively, a constitution that is frail and weak can easily succumb to cold, leading to prolapse of the large intestine.

    In children, diarrhea and dysentery are often caused by damp heat and wind-heat, which take advantage of a weakened spleen and stomach. Wind belongs to wood, and wood conquering suppresses earth, which governs the spleen and stomach—when they are weakened, they are easily subdued. Moreover, dampness tends to harm the spleen, and due to this weakness, it cannot discern the clear from the turbid. When food and water mix improperly, it results in profuse leakage; when this persists, the large intestine becomes weak.

    The large intestine is associated with the hand yangming metal; however, if earth is weak, it cannot generate metal. Once the energy of metal becomes deficient, the pathways of transmission are also weakened and may be struck by cold wind, causing the anus to prolapse and fail to retract.

    The treatment should aim to nourish the spleen and warm the stomach, allowing the metal to benefit from its mother and restore its energy. Formulas like Huo Xiang Tang, Yun Qi San, and Ping Wei San are advised. Subsequently, internal remedies to fortify the intestines can be given, such as Jian Pi Yin and Yang Zang Tang. Externally, methods like application of Fu Long Gan San and Bi Ma Gao at the rectal area can be used to uplift energy and encourage retraction; if retraction is achieved, wash off the remaining substances with water. Additionally, if there is pathogenic heat stagnating in the large intestine that has not been cleared, this condition may also arise.[19p]
    The anus is red and soft, the lung pulse is superficial and rapid, the fingerprints on the right hand are purple, the body is slightly warm, and there is occasional restlessness. First, administer the Clear Lung Drink for relief; then use Peppermint Powder and Panlong Powder for treatment, also taking Wanan Drink intermittently.

    Chao states: When there is excess heat, constipation occurs; when there is deficiency cold, the anus may prolapse. This often results from vomiting and diarrhea leading to a deficiency in spleen Qi, which fails to nourish the lungs, causing the Qi of the large intestine to weaken and descend. Use the Baizhong Yiqi Decoction or the Four Gentlemen Decoction as a primary treatment. If there is prolapse that is bright red or causes pain, it indicates blood deficiency with heat; use Baizhong Yiqi Decoction supplemented with Siwu Decoction and Peony Root. If there is slight redness or pain, it indicates Qi deficiency with heat; supplement with the Four Gentlemen Decoction and Peony Root. Generally, if the hands and feet are warm, it relates to gastric heat; if they are cold, it relates to gastric cold.[20p]
    The Tang family's method for treating rectal prolapse involves using scallion soup for steaming and washing to soften the condition, gently encouraging it back. This occurs following severe diarrhea; therefore, one may also take medicines for diarrhea, and then use sophora flowers and other herbs. Additionally, there is a method involving a decoction of sumac, combined with alumen for steaming and contraction. Another approach is to finely grind true cattail pollen, mix it with pig liver, apply it to the anus, and insert it. The "Complete Infants’ Prescription" suggests using the "Thin Intestine Powder." For those who also experience hemorrhoids with swelling and pain, a mixture of yellow lead and talc can be used, adjusted with well water for application, which will reduce the condition; also, using half a qian of white lead powder and half a character of brain powder mixed with good wine applied to the swollen area works well. Huanglian Jiedu Decoction can also be taken, and using a bitter kyanite decoction for washing is effective. There are also applications using myrobalan, white alum, and ground brain powder, followed by washing with substances like schizopepan and saposhnikovia. Using the root of raw trichosanthes is also beneficial.[21p]
    Discussion on Children's Health: Eight Types of Dysentery

    Children have weak and tender vital energy and blood, with soft internal organs. When exposed to wind and cold or consuming food that is too hot or too cold, they can be harmed by external pathogens, leading to disharmony in the spleen and stomach. This results in the stagnation of food and fluid, forming toxins and obstructions. It may manifest as an inability to absorb food or as a mixture of pus and blood, transforming into dysentery. There are eight types of dysentery:

    1. Watery Dysentery: Characterized by thin, watery stools that do not coalesce, the passage of which is frequent and urgent, indicating unprocessed food.

    2. Cold Dysentery: Identified by the passage of pure white pus.

    3. Hot Dysentery: Marked by the passage of pure red blood.

    4. Stagnant Dysentery: Involves stools that contain a mixture of pus and blood.

    5. Accumulation Dysentery: Results from an accumulation injury, which may improve temporarily but can recur.

    6. Consumption Dysentery: Occurs when consumption is present, leading to dysentery.

    7. Gu Dysentery: Resembles the effects of poison, resulting in purple or black blood, or resembling red bean juice or chicken and duck liver.

    8. Rest Inflicted Dysentery: Characterized by dark blood mixed with white substances, resembling fat from the intestines or the appearance of rotten fish intestines. This indicates ulceration of the intestines and stomach, and the patient should refrain from excessive concern, hence the name.

    It is also referred to as "rest inflicted" because the affliction may lead to death without any respite. If dysentery patients cannot ingest gruel or medicine, it signals a condition nearing death.[22p]
    Recipe for Da Huang Decoction

    This formula treats children who suffer from acute cold, digestive troubles due to food and water; if the milk is cold causing discomfort and not digesting; or if there is vomiting with distress due to cold stagnation, whether red or white, it is effective. If previously taken purgative formulas have led to an empty, cold stomach, resulting in watery stools, dry heaving, sunken eyes, and persistent distress unsuitable for further purging, one may use Da Huang. If nursing mothers have not cleared their water qi before feeding the child, and the child develops diarrhea, simply use Da Huang. For children with diarrhea who require assistance, use Da Huang; for those who do not need it and should be treated gently, it should be avoided.

    Ingredients:

    • Da Huang (six parts)
    • Gui Xin (one part)
    • Hou Po (one part)
    • Gan Cao (one part)
    • Gan Jiang (one part)
    • Ren Shen (two parts)
    • Fu Ling (two parts)
    • Bai Zhu (two parts)
    • Dang Gui (two parts)
    • Jie Geng (three parts)

    Combine these ten ingredients with three and a half sheng of water, then boil to obtain eight he. For children aged 30 to 60 days, give two he per dose; for those 70 to 100 days, two and a half he; for those over 200 days, three he per dose.[23p]
    Huangbo Decoction is for treating children who suffer from sudden cold in the summer, where cold counteracts severe heat, causing heat to enter the stomach, leading to red and white stagnation like fish brain, with intense heat, headaches, body heat, and irritated hands and feet. This is caused by the exterior cold injuring the Yang energy, allowing the heat to enter the stomach. Taking this remedy is beneficial. If one mistakenly uses purgative drugs or warm spleen decoctions, it will exacerbate the heat. If purgatives are used, it may lead to frequent diarrhea with red stools resembling rotten meat, or it may not heal even if purged; in that case, stronger heat-clearing drugs should be used. If the diarrhea does not stop and heat becomes more intense, taking this remedy will have immediate effects. If it is a warm disease with severe heat that encounters sudden cold, causing heat to enter the abdomen and resulting in bloody stools like fish brain, this remedy is effective.

    Ingredients: Huangbo, Huanglian, Shengma, Danggui, Bai Tou Weng (also known as Bai Lian), Muli, Pomegranate peel, Huangqin, Jishi, and Licorice, each 2 fen; Xijiao and Ai Ye, each 1 fen.

    These twelve ingredients should be crushed and boiled in three sheng of water until one sheng and two ge remain. For children aged 100 days to 200 days, take three and a half ge per dose.[24p]
    To treat the rectum and colon conditions in children suffering from dampness and cold, experiencing diarrhea with red, white, or green colors resembling fish brains, with rectal prolapse, persistent abdominal pain over time, you should use the following ingredients:

    • 0.5 qian of red stone resin
    • 0.3 qian of Wu Zhu Yu (dried fruit of the Evodia rutaecarpa)
    • Dried ginger
    • Aconite
    • Angelica
    • Magnolia bark
    • White attractor (Atractylodes)
    • Magnolia flower bark
    • White-headed crowfoot (Pulsatilla)
    • Coptis
    • Pomegranate peel
    • Chinese goldthread (Coptis chinensis), each 0.2 qian

    Grind these twelve ingredients into a fine powder, then mix with honey to form pills the size of soybeans. For a two-year-old, administer five pills, for ages three and up, ten pills, and for ages ten and up, twenty pills. For those with sudden diarrhea, take a small amount to ensure recovery; for those with persistent diarrhea, take the full dose again for optimal effect.[25p]
    Gardenia Pill: Cures persistent heat dysentery in children.

    Ingredients: Seven gardenia fruits, four jujubes (blackened), five parts Coptis chinensis, four parts alum stone, and three parts yellow brew. Grind these five ingredients into a fine powder. Make into pills the size of small beans. Take five pills three times a day and two at night; if unsure, increase to ten pills.

    Cilantro Round: Cures clear dysentery in children.

    Ingredients: Two parts cilantro, three parts Coptis chinensis, and one part Aconitum. Grind these three ingredients into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of mustard seeds. Take two pills with porridge and you will be cured immediately.

    Four Ingredients Liang Rice Soup: Cures excess watery diarrhea.

    Ingredients: Two sheng each of Liang rice, rice, and millet, and wax the size of a bullet. Combine these four ingredients with five sheng of water, boil Liang rice three times and strain, then use the broth to boil rice three times and strain, and likewise for millet. Mix the wax into the strained broth, and after the wax dissolves, drink it. Test it several times for efficacy.

    Dragon Bone Soup: Cures severe hot dysentery accompanied by excessive drinking.

    Ingredients: Two liang each of dragon bone, licorice, rhubarb, red resin, gypsum, cold water stone, trichosanthes root, and cinnamon. These eight ingredients are prepared for diarrhea treatment. Mix each with half a sheng of wine and water, boil down to two cups, strain, and dose according to the child's size.[26p]
    Da Huang Decoction: Treats slight diarrhea in young children, bitterness and heat leading to lack of appetite, and injuries affecting feeding. Ingredients: Da Huang, Gan Cao, Mai Men Dong, each 1 liang.

    Prepare by chewing these three ingredients, adding 2 sheng of water, and boiling down to 1 sheng. For children aged 2-3 years, divide into 3-4 doses.

    Sheng Jin Niu Huang Decoction: Treats persistent diarrhea due to accumulation in young children, resulting in convulsions. Ingredients: Sheng Jin, 3 zhu; 6 zhu for one formula, and roasted Jin can also be used. The method should produce powder; for those already fully prepared, use 3 zhu of Niu Huang, 2 fen of Ma Huang, 1 fen each of Huang Lian, Gan Jiang, Ren Shen, Gan Cao; ½ fen of Xi Xin.

    Chew these eight ingredients, add 1 sheng of water, boil down to 8 he, strain, and before serving, grind Niu Huang into the decoction. If the child seems hot, use fresh ginger instead of dry ginger. In contemporary times, if Sheng Jin is scarce, using the prepared ones is also fine; both 2-3 liang can be used.

    Ze Qi Zhi Yu Decoction: Treats children in summer suffering from sudden cold causing severe watery diarrhea. If cold penetrates the stomach, limbs may feel cold leading to strong fever that doesn't subside for days or even months, resulting in a feeling of fullness in the abdomen with a weak and fine pulse. Taking this decoction once can gradually calm the mind.

    Ingredients: Ze Qi, Qing Mu Xiang, Hai Zao, each 2 fen; Wu Zhi Yu, Fu Ling, Bai Zhu, Ku Geng, Shao Yao, Dang Gui, each 3 fen; Da Huang, 1 fen.

    Chew these ten ingredients, add 4 sheng of water, boil down to 1.5 sheng. For children from 200 days to 1 year, take 2.5 he; for those over 1 year up to 2 years, take 4 he.[27p]
    Zhi Shi San: For treating persistent diarrhea and urinary issues in children, where food intake is unbalanced, and the body is weak, this is advisable.

    Ingredients: 2 liang of Zhi Shi. For children aged three years and older, take a dose of the size of a thumb's breadth; for younger children, adjust the dosage accordingly. Administer three times a day.

    Gui Tou Yuan: For treating children with persistent cold accumulation that has not healed, and for cases of prolapse that are not healing, with abdominal cold and painful rectal area that prevents entry.

    Ingredients: 2 dead turtle heads, roasted until charred; 4 liang of magnetite; 3 liang of cinnamon heart; 1 piece of hedgehog skin, roasted until charred.

    Grind these four ingredients into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of broad beans. For children aged three to five years, take five to ten pills three times a day. Adjust the number for older children as needed.

    Chu Re Jie Chang Yuan: For children with yellow, red, or foamy diarrhea due to heat, with blood mixed with fish heads, and with ulcerations in the rectum, causing worms to breed.

    Ingredients: 0.5 liang each of Huang Lian, Bo He, Ku Shen, Gui Jiu, Du Huo, Ju Pi, Shao Yao, and Ejiao.

    Grind these eight ingredients into a powder, mix with indigo juice and honey to form pills the size of small beans. Take five to ten pills a day. In winter, if indigo juice is unavailable, use one measure of indigo powder, mixed with honey for pill-making.[28p]
    Xianglian Pills (from "True Formulas")
    Treats both red and white dysentery, as well as diarrhea due to heat and summer.
    20 taels of Huanglian,
    10 taels of Wuzhuyu (dried evodia fruit, stalks removed).
    First, mix the two ingredients with hot water, place in a ceramic container, and rest in hot water for one day. Then stir-fry until Huanglian turns purplish-yellow, remove the Wuzhu, and grind the Huanglian into powder. For every one part of powdered Huanglian, add one tael of powdered Muxiang and form into balls the size of sesame seeds using light vinegar and rice drink.

    Treats dysentery in children.

    ½ tael of Hezhi fruit pulp,
    ½ tael of licorice,
    2 qian of Clove.
    Grind these into a fine powder, take 2 qian each time, decoct in water, and take before meals.

    Xianglian Pills

    ½ tael of stir-fried Huanglian,
    1 qian of Longgu (dragon bone).
    Grind these into a fine powder, form into pills the size of millet, and take 20 pills with rice drink soup.

    Danxi Formula (from "Píanfāng Huìcuì", same below)
    Treats food accumulation dysentery.

    Recipe for Treating Food-Accumulation Diarrhea

    Fried Qū (a fermented grain product), Cāng Zhú (Atractylodes), Huá Shí (Talc), Sháo Yào (Peony), Huáng Qín (Scutellaria), Bái Zhú (Atractylodes), Gān Cǎo (Licorice), Chén Pí (Dried Citrus Peel), Fú Líng (Poria). Grind the above, and decoct with Bǎo Hé Wán (a medicinal pill).

    Er Zhú Soup treats children under eight with pure blood diarrhea due to food accumulation. Ingredients: Cāng Zhú, Bái Zhú, Huáng Qīn, Bái Sháo, Huá Shí, Fú Líng, Gān Cǎo, Chén Pí, and fried Shén Qū. Grind and decoct with Bǎo Hé Wán.

    Sān Huáng Wán
    Ingredients: Huāng Lián (Coptis), Huáng Qīn, Dà Huáng (Rhubarb). Grind together into a powder, form into pills with Shén Qū paste, and take with wood fragrance and betel nut decoction.

    Ingredients: Zhǐ Ké (Bitter Orange), Hòu Pò (Magnolia Bark), Dà Huáng, Máng Xiāo (Mirabilite), Gān Cǎo, Bīng Láng (Betel Nut). Make a dose from the above; this is a remedy for unblocking the intestines and eliminating accumulation.

    Bǎo Hé Wán
    Ingredients: 2 liang of Nán Shān Zhā Ròu (Hawthorn Fruit), fried Shén Qū, 1 liang each of Bàn Xià (Pinellia), Bái Fú Líng (White Poria), Bái Zhú, and 5 qian each of Luó Bo Zǐ (Radish Seeds), Lián Qiáo (Forsythia), and Chén Pí. Grind to powder, make into small pills the size of millet, and swallow with liquid. This is suitable for children with food accumulation and spleen deficiency.

    Tiao Zhong Tang
    To treat the end of summer and beginning of autumn, if one is suddenly struck by excessive heat, causing heat to constrict the limbs leading to high fever and headaches, or if cold harms the stomach resulting in dysentery with red or white stools.

It aids quick relief of symptoms, alleviates fever, and reduces significant heat.     Shilian San: This treats children with mouth-locking dysentery, nausea, and loss of appetite that comes and goes. Ingredients: Fried lotus seeds without heart.[34p]
    The first recipe is for treating diarrhea in children with the use of a meat powder mixed with rice drink. Use one tael of fine pork, slice it thinly, and mix with one qian of fatty powder. Roast the meat slowly over coals, then sprinkle with the fatty powder to make dried meat. Give a small amount to eat. If the child refuses, place it near their nose, and they will naturally want to eat it. This remedy is remarkable for curing toxic appetite.

    The next recipe is for a pill called "Fragrant Dried Drug," which treats accumulated diarrhea and dysentery. It requires one tael each of yellow vine and dried evodia, with the evodia stir-fried off; two and a half qian of wood fragrance; and half a tael of terminalia. Grind these into powder, mix with flour to form pills the size of sesame seeds, and take thirty pills with plain rice drink.

    The "Yellow Vine and Fragrant Herb Drink" treats heat-induced diarrhea with red stools. The ingredients include half a tael each of fried broad beans and roasted magnolia bark, one tael each of stir-fried yellow vine and ginger juice, and one tael of fragrant herb. This is ground into powder, and three qian should be taken with ginger water.

    The "Mao Flower Decoction" treats persistent nosebleeds and bleeding from the mouth or rectum. Use a large handful of mao flower, boil it with three cups of water until reduced to one cup, divide it into two doses for healing. If flowers are not available, use the roots and stalks instead. It also treats bloody dysentery.

    The last recipe, "Instant Stopping Pill," is a primary drug for treating severe diarrhea. One tael of yellow lead, forty-nine pieces of ban zhi (croton seed), and two qian of frankincense should be used. Mix with two qian of sesame oil and half a tael of wax, and form into pills. If cold symptoms are present, add two and a half qian of wood fragrance.[35p]
    Baidusan: Treats seasonal febrile diseases with symptoms of headache, stiff neck, severe heat with aversion to cold, and general body aches; also helps with coughing due to cold obstruction and heavy nasal congestion.

    Ingredients: Ginseng, Poria, Raw Licorice, Qianhu, Chuanxiong, Qianghuo, Duhuo, Platycodon, Chaihu, Stir-fried Bitter Orange Peel, each one tael.

    Wei Feng Tang: Treats wind-cold invading the stomach and intestines, food not digesting, diarrhea, abdominal sounds, fullness and pain, or with stool resembling bean juice or blood stasis, day and night without regulation.
    Ingredients: White peony, Atractylodes, cinnamon, ginseng, angelica, Chuanxiong, and Poria.
    Grind into powder, take 2 qian, mix with millet, decoct in water, take warm on an empty stomach.[37p]
    Di Yu Yin: Treats cold and hot dysentery, abdominal pain, and frequent red and white diarrhea.
    Combine three parts of Di Yu, two parts each of licorice, fried red peony, and bitter orange peel.
    Decoct in water for consumption.

    Sheng Yang Yi Wei Tang: Quenches thirst, relieves heat, and generates body fluids.
    Two qian of Huang Qi, one qian each of Ban Xia, Ren Shen, roasted licorice, Bai Zhu, and Chuan Huang Lian; five fen each of Chuan Du Huo, Fang Feng, Bai Shao, and Qiang Huo; three fen each of Chen Pi, Fu Ling, Chai Hu, and Ze Xie.
    Decoct in two sheng of water with three slices of ginger and two dates, boil down to four parts for consumption away from meals.

    Qiang Huo San: Treats wind-cold, headache, fever, bodily aches, phlegm obstruction cough, loss of voice, nasal congestion, heavy voice, and also alleviates intermittent dysentery (red and white).
    One liang each of Ren Shen, Qiang Huo, red Fu Ling, Chai Hu, Qian Hu, Chuan Xiong, Du Huo, and Jie Geng; fried bitter orange peel until light yellow, remove husk; Bai Zhu soaked overnight in rice wash, remove coarse skin and filter dry, then fry until light yellow; licorice.
    Grind all together, take two qian with one cup of water, three slices of ginger, and three leaves of mint, boil down to seven parts for consumption at any time when warm. Disperses wind pathogens, can be boiled with green onion. For dysentery, use ginger and rice wash for decoction.[38p]
    Soaked Cinnabar is a leading remedy for diarrhea and dysentery. Grind cinnabar finely, using one tael. Take twenty-five large colocynths, remove the skin and membrane, and grind out the oil. Mix thoroughly with half a tael of yellow wax, melt to a liquid, and blend evenly. Shape into pills of appropriate size, soak in water, and swallow. Use as needed when illness occurs. Another method uses two and a half taels of cinnabar.

    Wide Intestine Pill treats urgent diarrhea after dysentery and unblocking issues of the large intestine. Stir-fry the bitter orange peel until slightly yellow, then soak one tael in clear oil to saturate, dry it out. Use five qian of shelled hemp seeds, wood unblock, half raw and half burnt rhubarb, betel nut, and dried large belly peel. Use two and a half qian of each. Except for the hemp seeds, grind very finely in a mortar. Mix the other five ingredients, ensuring the betel nut is not overheated, then dry and grind to a powder. Combine in the mortar with the hemp seeds and grind again. Shape into pills the size of small beans, taking thirty to fifty pills at a time, using a decoction of bitter orange peel and licorice to wash down, preferably on an empty stomach. For infants aged one to two years, use warm honey soup to administer.

    Earth Yarrow Powder contains equal parts of earth yarrow, Terminalia chebula, Magnolia bark, and ginger. Grind to a powder, taking two qian per dose, mixed with one cup of water, and boiled with ginger and jujube for drinking.

    Another formula consists of equal parts of earth yarrow, black plum, medicinal peel, licorice, and angelica. Grind to a powder, taking two qian per dose, boiled in water for consumption.[39p]

      Wu Mei San: Treats children's heat dysentery, especially with strong fever and excessive thirst, when dysentery does not stop. Use two pieces of dried black plum (Wu Mei), lightly roasted; a small amount of yellow dawn (Huang Lian), lightly roasted; one part of blue leaves (Lan Ye); shavings of rhinoceros horn; crushed donkey-hide gelatin (A Jiao), roasted until yellowed; half a portion each of honey-fried licorice. Grind the above ingredients roughly, then create a powder. Take one qian (a weight unit) each time, using a small cup of water, decoct until reduced to one-fifth, strain, let cool, and adjust the dosage according to the child's size.

    Kai Wei San: Treats red dysentery. Use half a qian each of white atractylodes (Bai Zhu), poria (Fu Ling), and ginseng (Ren Shen); ten lotus seeds (Shi Lian Zi). Grind into a powder and take half a qian with a decoction of fragrant angelica (Huo Xiang).

    Yang Zang Tang: For generating fluids and boosting energy, warming the intestines and stopping dysentery. Use two and a half qian each of ginseng (Ren Shen) and honey-fried licorice (Zhi Gan Cao); half a liang (another weight unit) of white peony (Bai Shao) and white atractylodes (Bai Zhu); one qian each of southwood (Nan Mu Xiang) and cinnamon (Rou Gui) with rough bark removed; one and a half qian each of roasted nutmeg (Rou Dou Kou) and poppy seed shells (Ying Su Ke) with the hull removed and stir-fried with honey water; one and a half qian of myrobalan (He Zi). Grind all these ingredients, taking two qian at a time, with a cup of water, two slices of ginger, and one jujube; decoct to seven parts, and take warm on an empty stomach; optionally, decoct with rice.

    Guang Ji Fang: For treating cold white dysentery. Use six fen (a smaller weight unit) of ginseng (Ren Shen); four fen each of roasted magnolia bark (Hou Po) and roasted licorice (Gan Cao); five fen each of poria (Fu Ling) and platycodon (Jie Geng); eight fen of roasted zelkova bark (Liang Zhou Ju Pi). Cut all six ingredients, boil with three sheng (a larger volume unit) of water to yield one sheng, adjust the dosage to one cup, and cease treatment when symptoms resolve. Avoid according to common methods.[41p]

    Xiang Lian Pill: Treats both red and white diarrhea, thirst, and pain.

    Ingredients:
    1 tael of prepared Huang Lian (Coptis), finely chopped, stir-fried with Wu Zhu Yu (Evodia) until fragrant, then remove the Wu Zhu Yu;
    2.5 qian of dried Wu Mei meat, thinly sliced and slowly roasted on a new tile;
    0.5 tael of Nan Mu Xiang (Cardamom); do not overheat.

    Grind these into powder. Use 0.5 tael of prepared E Jiao (Colla Corii Asini), finely chopped, stir-fry until puffed, then hydrate with water to form a paste. Once cooled, combine with the previous powder, mix thoroughly in a mortar, and form into pills the size of hemp seeds.     San Shuang Pills treat children's red-white or mixed diarrhea in five colors.
    Remove the skin from three qian of good quality white banana seeds and grind them finely.     • Yellow Lead, calcined, each two qian (a unit of weight)
    • Three pieces of Heshou (Chebula), cooked thoroughly

    Grind the above into powder. For each dose, take half a qian mixed with gruel drink. For those over three years, use half a qian.

    Fermented Milk Method:
    Treats children's tight mouth dysentery.

    • Thick Magnolia Bark
    • Zhi Ke (bitter orange), five fen each
    • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes)

    Resting Dysentery Prescription

    From "Zhou Hou," for treating persistent dysentery.

    Dragon bone, roasted until yellow and charred, pounded and taken in a dose the size of a thumb, three times a day will bring recovery.

    Another Prescription:
    Four ounces of dragon bone, pounded to the size of small beans, boiled in five liters of water until reduced to two and a half liters, cooled, and divided into five doses, will be effective.

    Preserving Life Trustworthy Efficacious Muffins: For treating all forms of lumps, accumulations, stagnation, and other conditions persisting for ten to twenty years.

    Roasted fine ink, bitter herbs, soaked and stir-fried until charred, green stone, large dragon, stir-fried lacquer, five spirit resin, Beijing three-edge, mugwort, myrrh, tangerine peel, roasted oyster shell, each half an ounce. Fourteen large dates, roasted; one ounce of cleaned castor bean, wrapped in damp paper, burned until charred and stopped; white丁香, grinding antimony; wingless and legless蝱虫; one part each of spotted cat.

    Combine all into a fine powder, cook with vinegar to make dough balls the size of soap, form into muffins, and administer with the broth of the affected substance or warm flour soup. They must be chewed and swallowed; as the accumulation gradually shifts downward, take another ball when it moves further down. If normal circulation is needed, administer with flour soup. Blood clots, blockages, and persistent dysentery with pus and blood in both adults and children can all be treated here.[55p]
    Jade Command Dan: Treats children suffering from long-term red and white dysentery, and those with persistent dysentery and weak stomachs, who are increasingly emaciated, have furrowed brows, eat excessive earth, and refuse food.

    Ingredients:

    • Half a tael each of ground sulfur, Mitra, and yellow lead.
    • Two taels each of ground cold water stone and white alum.
    • Prepared salt mud must be used for solidifying and dripping, and red calcined to be ground with musk as one character.

    Mix these six ingredients evenly. Form into small pills the size of mung beans. Each dose is ten pills, taken with a decoction of black plums and licorice. Adjust dosage for children. Avoid raw, cold, poisonous substances and moldy foods.

    Thousand Gold Gu Poison Dysentery Formula: Treats lower blood, appearing like chicken liver, with intolerable abdominal pain, called Gu poison dysentery.

    Ingredients:

    • Three taels each of madder root, bulbus, and rhinoceros horn.
    • Two taels each of balloon flower, yellow barberry, and golden shield.
    • Four taels each of earth’s yew and white lotus root.

    Crush these eight ingredients and infuse in nine liters of water, then boil down to two and a half liters, divided into three doses. This is for Gu poison dysentery, with reduced dosage for children.[56p]
    Prescription for Treating Gu Li (Dysentery)

    Dry the leaves of the cypress and grind them into a powder, combine with equal parts of Sichuan Huanglian.

    Boil these two ingredients together to extract the juice, and administer it to treat children's severe abdominal pain, expelling black blood, tea-colored stool, or pus-like blood resembling sediment, known as gu li. This treatment is highly effective and can also eliminate the five organ toxins.

    Shenghui Pervinca Powder

    For treating persistent gu poison dysentery in children, characterized by heat and restlessness in the body.

    Ingredients: 2 taels of white pervinca root, 2 taels of ageratum, 1 fen of roasted drum skin (burnt), 0.5 taels of roasted licorice, 0.5 taels of dried blue leaf, and 0.3 taels of red peony and rhino horn shavings.

    Crush these herbs and sieve them to create a powder. For each dose, take 1 qian (approximately 3 grams), mix with a small cup of water and add 27 grains of fermented soybean, boil until reduced to one-fifth. Strain the mixture and give it warm, adjusting the dosage based on the child's size.

    Crush these herbs and sieve them to make a powder. For each dose, take 1 qian, mix with a small cup of water, boil until it reduces to one-fifth, strain, and allow it to cool, adjusting dosage according to the child's size.[57p]
